States state symbols">\n          Lists of United States state symbols\n         </a>\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n      </table>\n      <p>\n       <b>\n        Delaware\n       </b>\n       (\n       <span class="nowrap">\n        <span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt">\n         <a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">\n          /\n          <span style="border-bottom:1px dotted">\n           <span title="/\xcb\x88/: primary stress follows">\n            \xcb\x88\n           </span>\n           <span title="\'d\' in \'dye\'">\n            d\n           </span>\n           <span title="/\xc9\x9b/: \'e\' in \'dress\'">\n            \xc9\x9b\n           </span>\n           <span title="\'l\' in \'lie\'">\n            l\n           </span>\n           <span title="/\xc9\x99/: \'a\' in \'about\'">\n            \xc9\x99\n           </span>\n           <span title="\'w\' in \'wind\'">\n            w\n           </span>\n           <span title="/\xc9\x9b\xc9\x99r/: \'are\' in \'bare\'">\n            \xc9\x9b\xc9\x99r\n           </span>\n          </span>\n          /\n         </a>\n        </span>\n        <small class="nowrap">\n         (\n         <span class="unicode haudio">\n          <span class="fn">\n           <span style="white-space:nowrap">\n            <a href="/wiki/File:En-us-Delaware.ogg" title="About this sound">\n             <img alt="About this sound" data-file-height="20" data-file-width="20" height="11" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/11px-Loudspeaker.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/17px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/22px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 2x" width="11"/>\n            </a>\n           </span>\n           <a class="internal" href="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/e/e6/En-us-Delaware.ogg" title="En-us-Delaware.ogg">\n            listen\n           </a>\n          </span>\n         </span>\n         )\n        </small>\n       </span>\n       )\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9">\n        <a href="#cite_note-9">\n         [9]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       is a\n       <a href="/wiki/U.S._state" title="U.S. state">\n        state\n       </a>\n       located in the\n       <a href="/wiki/Mid-Atlantic_states" title="Mid-Atlantic states">\n        Mid-Atlantic\n       </a>\n       or\n       <a href="/wiki/Northeastern_United_States" title="Northeastern United States">\n        Northeastern\n       </a>\n       regions of the\n       <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">\n        United States\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WhichRegion_10-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-WhichRegion-10">\n         [a]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       It is bordered to the south and west by\n       <a href="/wiki/Maryland" title="Maryland">\n        Maryland\n       </a>\n       , to the northeast by\n       <a href="/wiki/New_Jersey" title="New Jersey">\n        New Jersey\n       </a>\n       , and to the north by\n       <a href="/wiki/Pennsylvania" title="Pennsylvania">\n        Pennsylvania\n       </a>\n       . The state takes its name from\n       <a href="/wiki/Thomas_West,_3rd_Baron_De_La_Warr" title="Thomas West, 3rd Baron De La Warr">\n        Thomas West, 3rd Baron De La Warr\n       </a>\n       , an English nobleman and\n       <a href="/wiki/Virginia" title="Virginia">\n        Virginia\n       </a>\n       \'s first colonial governor.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11">\n        <a href="#cite_note-11">\n         [10]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Delaware occupies the northeastern portion of the\n       <a href="/wiki/Delmarva_Peninsula" title="Delmarva Peninsula">\n        Delmarva Peninsula\n       </a>\n       and is the\n       <a href="/wiki/List_of_U.S._states_and_territories_by_area" title="List of U.S. states and territories by area">\n        second smallest\n       </a>\n       , the\n       <a href="/wiki/List_of_U.S._states_and_territories_by_population" title="List of U.S. states and territories by population">\n        sixth least populous\n       </a>\n       , but the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_U.S._states_and_territories_by_population_density" title="List of U.S. states and territories by population density">\n        sixth most densely populated\n       </a>\n       of the 50 United States. Delaware is divided into\n       <a href="/wiki/List_of_counties_in_Delaware" title="List of counties in Delaware">\n        three counties\n       </a>\n       , the lowest number of counties of any state. From north to south, the three counties are\n       <a href="/wiki/New_Castle_County,_Delaware" title="New Castle County, Delaware">\n        New Castle\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Kent_County,_Delaware" title="Kent County, Delaware">\n        Kent\n       </a>\n       , and\n       <a href="/wiki/Sussex_County,_Delaware" title="Sussex County, Delaware">\n        Sussex\n       </a>\n       . While the southern two counties have historically been predominantly agricultural, New Castle County has been more industrialized.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Before its coastline was explored by Europeans in the 16th century, Delaware was inhabited by several groups of Native Americans, including the\n       <a href="/wiki/Lenape" title="Lenape">\n        Lenape\n       </a>\n       in the north and\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nanticoke_Indian_Tribe" title="Nanticoke Indian Tribe">\n        Nanticoke\n       </a>\n       in the south. It was initially colonized by\n       <a href="/wiki/Dutch_people" title="Dutch people">\n        Dutch\n       </a>\n       traders at\n       <a href="/wiki/Zwaanendael_Colony" title="Zwaanendael Colony">\n        Zwaanendael\n       </a>\n       , near the present town of\n       <a href="/wiki/Lewes,_Delaware" title="Lewes, Delaware">\n        Lewes\n       </a>\n       , in 1631.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12">\n        <a href="#cite_note-12">\n         [11]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Delaware was one of the\n       <a href="/wiki/Thirteen_Colonies" title="Thirteen Colonies">\n        13 colonies\n       </a>\n       participating in the\n       <a href="/wiki/American_Revolution" title="American Revolution">\n        American Revolution\n       </a>\n       . On December\xc2\xa07, 1787, Delaware became the first state to ratify the\n       <a href="/wiki/United_States_Constitution" title="United States Constitution">\n        Constitution of the United States\n       </a>\n       , and has since been known as\n       <i>\n        "The First State"\n       </i>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13">\n        <a href="#cite_note-13">\n         [12]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n      </p>\n      <div class="toc" id="toc">\n       <div class="toctitle">\n        <h2>\n         Contents\n      External links\n          </span>\n         </a>\n        </li>\n       </ul>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Etymology">\n        Etymology\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <p>\n       The state was named after the\n       <a href="/wiki/Delaware_River#Origin_of_the_name" title="Delaware River">\n        Delaware River\n       </a>\n       , which in turn derived its name from\n       <a href="/wiki/Thomas_West,_3rd_Baron_De_La_Warr" title="Thomas West, 3rd Baron De La Warr">\n        Thomas West, 3rd Baron De La Warr\n       </a>\n       (1577\xe2\x80\x931618) who was the ruling governor of the\n       <a href="/wiki/Colony_of_Virginia" title="Colony of Virginia">\n        Colony of Virginia\n       </a>\n       at the time Europeans first explored the river. The\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Delaware_Indians" title="Delaware Indians">\n        Delaware Indians\n       </a>\n       , a name used by\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Europeans" title="Europeans">\n        Europeans\n       </a>\n       for\n       <a href="/wiki/Lenape" title="Lenape">\n        Lenape\n       </a>\n       people indigenous to the Delaware Valley, also derive their name from the same source.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The surname\n       <i>\n        de La Warr\n       </i>\n       comes from\n       <a href="/wiki/Sussex" title="Sussex">\n        Sussex\n       </a>\n       and is of\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Anglo-Norman" title="Anglo-Norman">\n        Anglo-Norman\n       </a>\n       origin.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14">\n        <a href="#cite_note-14">\n         [13]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       It came probably from a Norman\n       <a href="/wiki/Lieu-dit" title="Lieu-dit">\n        lieu-dit\n       </a>\n       <i>\n        La Guerre\n       </i>\n       . This\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Toponymic" title="Toponymic">\n        toponymic\n       </a>\n       could derive from the Latin word\n       <i>\n        <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/ager#Latin" title="wikt:ager">\n         ager\n        </a>\n       </i>\n       , from the Breton\n       <i>\n        <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/gwern#Breton" title="wikt:gwern">\n         gwern\n        </a>\n       </i>\n       or from the\n       <a href="/wiki/Late_Latin" title="Late Latin">\n        Late Latin\n       </a>\n       <i>\n        varectum\n       </i>\n       (\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fallow" title="Fallow">\n        fallow\n       </a>\n       ). The toponyms Gara, Gare, Gaire (the sound\n       <a href="/wiki/Open_central_unrounded_vowel" title="Open central unrounded vowel">\n        [\xc3\xa4]\n       </a>\n       often mutated in\n       <a href="/wiki/Near-open_front_unrounded_vowel" title="Near-open front unrounded vowel">\n        [\xc3\xa6]\n       </a>\n       ) also appear in old texts cited by\n       <a href="/wiki/Lucien_Musset" title="Lucien Musset">\n        Lucien Musset\n       </a>\n       , where the word\n       <i>\n        ga(i)ra\n       </i>\n       means\n       <a href="/wiki/Gore_(road)" title="Gore (road)">\n        gore\n       </a>\n       . It could also be linked with a\n       <a href="/wiki/Patronymic" title="Patronymic">\n        patronymic\n       </a>\n       from the Old Norse\n       <i>\n        <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/verr#Old_Norse" title="wikt:verr">\n         verr\n        </a>\n       </i>\n       .\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">\n        Geography\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       Main articles:\n       <a href="/wiki/Twelve-Mile_Circle" title="Twelve-Mile Circle">\n        Twelve-Mile Circle\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Wedge_(border)" title="Wedge (border)">\n        Wedge (border)\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mason%E2%80%93Dixon_Line" title="Mason\xe2\x80\x93Dixon Line">\n        Mason\xe2\x80\x93Dixon Line\n       </a>\n       , and\n       <a href="/wiki/Transpeninsular_Line" title="Transpeninsular Line">\n        Transpeninsular Line\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       See also:\n       <a href="#Counties">\n        "Counties" section below\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;">\n        <a class="image" County, Delaware\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image"      </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Woodbrook_test.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1936" data-file-width="2592" height="164" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/81/Woodbrook_test.jpg/220px-Woodbrook_test.jpg"       <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Woodbrook_test.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         Sunset in Woodbrook, New Castle County, Delaware\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       Delaware is 96 miles (154\xc2\xa0km) long and ranges from 9 miles (14\xc2\xa0km) to 35 miles (56\xc2\xa0km) across, totaling 1,954 square miles (5,060\xc2\xa0km\n       <sup>\n        2\n       </sup>\n       ), making it the second-smallest state in the United States after\n       <a href="/wiki/Rhode_Island" title="Rhode Island">\n        Rhode Island\n       </a>\n       . Delaware is bounded to the north by\n       <a href="/wiki/Pennsylvania" title="Pennsylvania">\n        Pennsylvania\n       </a>\n       ; to the east by the\n       <a href="/wiki/Delaware_River" title="Delaware River">\n        Delaware River\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Delaware_Bay" title="Delaware Bay">\n        Delaware Bay\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/New_Jersey" title="New Jersey">\n        New Jersey\n       </a>\n       and the Atlantic Ocean; and to the west and south by\n       <a href="/wiki/Maryland" title="Maryland">\n        Maryland\n       </a>\n       . Small portions of Delaware are also situated on the eastern side of the Delaware River sharing land boundaries with New Jersey. The state of Delaware, together with the\n       <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Shore_of_Maryland" title="Eastern Shore of Maryland">\n        Eastern Shore counties of Maryland\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Shore_of_Virginia" title="Eastern Shore of Virginia">\n        two counties of Virginia\n       </a>\n       , form the\n       <a href="/wiki/Delmarva_Peninsula" title="Delmarva Peninsula">\n        Delmarva Peninsula\n       </a>\n       , which stretches down the Mid-Atlantic Coast.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The definition of the northern boundary of the state is unusual. Most of the boundary between Delaware and Pennsylvania was originally defined by an arc extending 12 miles (19.3\xc2\xa0km) from the\n       <a href="/wiki/Cupola" title="Cupola">\n        cupola\n       </a>\n       of the courthouse in the city of\n       <a href="/wiki/New_Castle,_Delaware" title="New Castle, Delaware">\n        New Castle\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">\n        [\n        <i>\n         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">\n          <span title="Need supporting reference for this claim (March 2016)">\n           citation needed\n          </span>\n         </a>\n        </i>\n        ]\n       </sup>\n       This boundary is often referred to as the\n       <a href="/wiki/Twelve-Mile_Circle" title="Twelve-Mile Circle">\n        Twelve-Mile Circle\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15">\n        <a href="#cite_note-15">\n         [b]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       This is the only nominally circular state boundary in the United States.\n       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">\n        [\n        <i>\n         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">\n          <span title="Need supporting reference for this claim (March 2016)">\n           citation needed\n          </span>\n         </a>\n        </i>\n        ]\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       This border extends all the way east to the low-tide mark on the New Jersey shore, then continues south along the shoreline until it again reaches the 12-mile (19\xc2\xa0km) arc in the south; then the boundary continues in a more conventional way in the middle of the main channel (\n       <a href="/wiki/Thalweg" title="Thalweg">\n        thalweg\n       </a>\n       ) of the Delaware River. To the west, a portion of the arc extends past the easternmost edge of Maryland. The remaining western border runs slightly east of due south from its intersection with the arc.\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/The_Wedge_(border)" title="The Wedge (border)">\n        The Wedge\n       </a>\n       of land between the northwest part of the arc and the Maryland border was claimed by both Delaware and Pennsylvania until 1921, when Delaware\'s claim was confirmed.\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Topography">\n        Topography\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <p>\n       Delaware is on a level plain, with the lowest mean elevation of any state in the nation.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-census_16-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-census-16">\n         [14]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Its highest elevation, located at\n       <a href="/wiki/Ebright_Azimuth" title="Ebright Azimuth">\n        Ebright Azimuth\n       </a>\n       , near\n       <a href="/wiki/Concord_High_School_(Wilmington,_Delaware)" title="Concord High School (Wilmington, Delaware)">\n        Concord High School\n       </a>\n       , doesn\'t quite reach 450 feet (140\xc2\xa0m) above sea level.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-census_16-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-census-16">\n         [14]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The northernmost part of the state is part of the\n       <a href="/wiki/Piedmont_(United_States)" title="Piedmont (United States)">\n        Piedmont Plateau\n       </a>\n       with hills and rolling surfaces. The\n       <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_Seaboard_fall_line" title="Atlantic Seaboard fall line">\n        Atlantic Seaboard fall line\n       </a>\n       approximately follows the\n       <a href="/wiki/Delaware_Route_2" title="Delaware Route 2">\n        Robert Kirkwood Highway\n       </a>\n       between\n       <a href="/wiki/Newark,_Delaware" title="Newark, Delaware">\n        Newark\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Wilmington,_Delaware" title="Wilmington, Delaware">\n        Wilmington\n       </a>\n       ; south of this road is the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Atlantic_Coastal_Plain" title="Atlantic Coastal Plain">\n        Atlantic Coastal Plain\n       </a>\n       with flat, sandy, and, in some parts, swampy ground.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17">\n        <a href="#cite_note-17">\n         [15]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       A ridge about 75 to 80 feet (23 to 24\xc2\xa0m) in elevation extends along the western boundary of the state and separates the\n       <a href="/wiki/Drainage_basin" title="Drainage basin">\n        watersheds\n       </a>\n       that feed Delaware River and Bay to the east and the\n       <a href="/wiki/Chesapeake_Bay" title="Chesapeake Bay">\n        Chesapeake Bay\n       </a>\n       to the west.\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Climate">\n        Climate\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <p>\n       Since almost all of Delaware is a part of the\n       <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_coastal_plain" title="Atlantic coastal plain">\n        Atlantic coastal plain\n       </a>\n       , the effects of the ocean moderate its climate. The state lies in the\n       <a href="/wiki/Humid_subtropical_climate" title="Humid subtropical climate">\n        humid subtropical climate\n       </a>\n       zone. Despite its small size (roughly 100 miles (160\xc2\xa0km) from its northernmost to southernmost points), there is significant variation in mean temperature and amount of snowfall between Sussex County and New Castle County. Moderated by the Atlantic Ocean and Delaware Bay, the southern portion of the state has a milder climate and a longer growing season than the northern portion of the state. Delaware\'s all-time record high of 110\xc2\xa0\xc2\xb0F (43\xc2\xa0\xc2\xb0C) was recorded at\n       <a href="/wiki/Millsboro,_Delaware" title="Millsboro, Delaware">\n        Millsboro\n       </a>\n       on July 21, 1930. The all-time record low of \xe2\x88\x9217\xc2\xa0\xc2\xb0F (\xe2\x88\x9227\xc2\xa0\xc2\xb0C) was also recorded at Millsboro on January 17, 1893.\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Environment">\n        Environment\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <p>\n       The transitional climate of Delaware supports a wide variety of vegetation. In the northern third of the state are found\n       <a href="/wiki/Northeastern_coastal_forests" title="Northeastern coastal forests">\n        Northeastern coastal forests\n       </a>\n       and mixed\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Quercus" title="Quercus">\n        oak\n       </a>\n       forests typical of the northeastern United States.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ecoregions_18-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-ecoregions-18">\n         [16]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       In the southern two-thirds of the state are found\n       <a href="/wiki/Middle_Atlantic_coastal_forests" title="Middle Atlantic coastal forests">\n        Middle Atlantic coastal forests\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ecoregions_18-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-ecoregions-18">\n         [16]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <a href="/wiki/Trap_Pond_State_Park" title="Trap Pond State Park">\n        Trap Pond State Park\n       </a>\n       , along with areas in other parts of Sussex County, for example, support the northernmost stands of\n       <a href="/wiki/Taxodium_distichum" title="Taxodium distichum">\n        bald cypress\n       </a>\n       trees in\n       <a href="/wiki/North_America" title="North America">\n        North America\n       </a>\n       .\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Environmental_management">\n        Environmental management\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <p>\n       Delaware provides\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Government_subsidy" title="Government subsidy">\n        government subsidy\n       </a>\n       support for the\n       <a href="/wiki/Environmental_remediation" title="Environmental remediation">\n        clean-up\n       </a>\n       of property "lightly contaminated" by\n       <a href="/wiki/Hazardous_waste" title="Hazardous waste">\n        hazardous waste\n       </a>\n       , the proceeds for which come from a tax on wholesale petroleum sales.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19">\n        <a href="#cite_note-19">\n         [17]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="History">\n        History\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       Main article:\n       <a href="/wiki/History_of_Delaware" title="History of Delaware">\n        History of Delaware\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Native_Americans">\n        Native Americans\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <p>\n       Before Delaware was settled by European colonists, the area was home to the Eastern\n       <a href="/wiki/Algonquian_peoples" title="Algonquian peoples">\n        Algonquian\n       </a>\n       tribes known as the Unami\n       <a href="/wiki/Lenape" title="Lenape">\n        Lenape\n       </a>\n       , or Delaware, who lived mostly along the coast, and the\n       <a href="/wiki/Nanticoke_people" title="Nanticoke people">\n        Nanticoke\n       </a>\n       who occupied much of the southern Delmarva Peninsula. John Smith also shows two Iroquoian tribes, the Kuskarawock &amp;\n       <a href="/wiki/Tockwogh" title="Tockwogh">\n        Tockwogh\n       </a>\n       , living north of the Nanticoke &amp; they may have held small portions of land in the western part of the state before migrating across the Chesapeake Bay.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20">\n        <a href="#cite_note-20">\n         [18]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The Kuskarawocks were most likely the\n       <a href="/wiki/Tuscarora_people" title="Tuscarora people">\n        Tuscarora\n       </a>\n       .\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The Unami Lenape in the Delaware Valley were closely related to\n       <a href="/wiki/Munsee" title="Munsee">\n        Munsee\n       </a>\n       Lenape tribes along the\n       <a href="/wiki/Hudson_River" title="Hudson River">\n        Hudson River\n       </a>\n       . They had a settled hunting and agricultural society, and they rapidly became middlemen in an increasingly frantic fur trade with their ancient enemy, the Minqua or\n       <a href="/wiki/Susquehannock" title="Susquehannock">\n        Susquehannock\n       </a>\n       . With the loss of their lands on the Delaware River and the destruction of the Minqua by the\n       <a href="/wiki/Iroquois" title="Iroquois">\n        Iroquois\n       </a>\n       of the Five Nations in the 1670s, the remnants of the Lenape who wished to remain identified as such left the region and moved over the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Alleghany_Mountains" title="Alleghany Mountains">\n        Alleghany Mountains\n       </a>\n       by the mid-18th century. Generally, those who did not relocate out of the state of Delaware were baptized, became Christian and were grouped together with other persons of color in official records and in the minds of their non-Native American neighbors.\n       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">\n        [\n        <i>\n         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">\n          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (January 2017)">\n           citation needed\n          </span>\n         </a>\n        </i>\n        ]\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Colonial_Delaware">\n        Colonial Delaware\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:NouvSuede.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1151" data-file-width="1146" height="201" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/57/NouvSuede.jpg/200px-NouvSuede.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/57/NouvSuede.jpg/300px-NouvSuede.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/57/NouvSuede.jpg/400px-NouvSuede.jpg 2x" width="200"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:NouvSuede.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         New Sweden \xe2\x80\x93 encounter between Swedish colonists and the natives of Delaware.\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       The\n       <a href="/wiki/Dutch_people" title="Dutch people">\n        Dutch\n       </a>\n       were the first Europeans to settle in present-day Delaware in the middle region by establishing a trading post at\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Zwaanendael,_Delaware" title="Zwaanendael, Delaware">\n        Zwaanendael\n       </a>\n       , near the site of\n       <a href="/wiki/Lewes,_Delaware" title="Lewes, Delaware">\n        Lewes\n       </a>\n       in 1631. Within a year all the settlers were killed in a dispute with\n       <a href="/wiki/Native_Americans_in_the_United_States" title="Native Americans in the United States">\n        area Native American tribes\n       </a>\n       . In 1638\n       <a href="/wiki/New_Sweden" title="New Sweden">\n        New Sweden\n       </a>\n       , a\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Swedish_people" title="Swedish people">\n        Swedish\n       </a>\n       trading post and colony, was established at\n       <a href="/wiki/Fort_Christina" title="Fort Christina">\n        Fort Christina\n       </a>\n       (now in\n       <a href="/wiki/Wilmington,_Delaware" title="Wilmington, Delaware">\n        Wilmington\n       </a>\n       ) by\n       <a href="/wiki/Peter_Minuit" title="Peter Minuit">\n        Peter Minuit\n       </a>\n       at the head of a group of Swedes,\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Finnish_people" title="Finnish people">\n        Finns\n       </a>\n       and Dutch. The colony of New Sweden lasted for 17 years. In 1651 the Dutch, reinvigorated by the leadership of\n       <a href="/wiki/Peter_Stuyvesant" title="Peter Stuyvesant">\n        Peter Stuyvesant\n       </a>\n       , established a fort at present-day\n       <a href="/wiki/New_Castle,_Delaware" title="New Castle, Delaware">\n        New Castle\n       </a>\n       , and in 1655 they conquered the New Sweden colony, annexing it into the Dutch\n       <a href="/wiki/New_Netherland" title="New Netherland">\n        New Netherland\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hod_21-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-hod-21">\n         [19]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22">\n        <a href="#cite_note-22">\n         [20]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Only nine years later, in 1664, the Dutch were conquered by a fleet of English ships by Sir Robert Carr under the direction of\n       <a href="/wiki/James_II_of_England" title="James II of England">\n        James, the Duke of York\n       </a>\n       . Fighting off a prior claim by\n       <a href="/wiki/Cecil_Calvert,_2nd_Baron_Baltimore" title="Cecil Calvert, 2nd Baron Baltimore">\n        Cecil Calvert, 2nd Baron Baltimore\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Province_of_Maryland" title="Province of Maryland">\n        Proprietor of Maryland\n       </a>\n       , the Duke passed his somewhat dubious ownership on to\n       <a href="/wiki/William_Penn" title="William Penn">\n        William Penn\n       </a>\n       in 1682. Penn strongly desired access to the sea for his\n       <a href="/wiki/Province_of_Pennsylvania" title="Province of Pennsylvania">\n        Pennsylvania province\n       </a>\n       and leased what then came to be known as the "Lower Counties on the Delaware"\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hod_21-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-hod-21">\n         [19]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       from the Duke.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Penn established representative government and briefly combined his two possessions under one General Assembly in 1682. However, by 1704 the Province of Pennsylvania had grown so large that their representatives wanted to make decisions without the assent of the Lower Counties and the two groups of representatives began meeting on their own, one at\n       <a href="/wiki/Philadelphia" title="Philadelphia">\n        Philadelphia\n       </a>\n       , and the other at New Castle. Penn and his heirs remained proprietors of both and always appointed the same person Governor for their Province of Pennsylvania and their territory of the Lower Counties. The fact that Delaware and Pennsylvania shared the same governor was not unique. From 1703 to 1738 New York and New Jersey shared a governor.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23">\n        <a href="#cite_note-23">\n         [21]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Massachusetts and New Hampshire also shared a governor for some time.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24">\n        <a href="#cite_note-24">\n         [22]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Dependent in early years on indentured labor, Delaware imported more slaves as the number of English\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Immigrants" title="Immigrants">\n        immigrants\n       </a>\n       decreased with better economic conditions in England. The colony became a slave society and cultivated tobacco as a cash crop, although English immigrants continued to arrive.\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="American_Revolution">\n        American Revolution\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <p>\n       Like the other middle colonies, the Lower Counties on the Delaware initially showed little enthusiasm for a break with\n       <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Great_Britain" title="Kingdom of Great Britain">\n        Britain\n       </a>\n       . The citizenry had a good relationship with the Proprietary government, and generally were allowed more independence of action in their Colonial Assembly than in other colonies. Merchants at the port of Wilmington had trading ties with the British.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       So it was that New Castle lawyer\n       <a href="/wiki/Thomas_McKean" title="Thomas McKean">\n        Thomas McKean\n       </a>\n       denounced the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Stamp_Act" title="Stamp Act">\n        Stamp Act\n       </a>\n       in the strongest terms, and Kent County native\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/John_Dickinson_(delegate)" title="John Dickinson (delegate)">\n        John Dickinson\n       </a>\n       became the "Penman of the Revolution." Anticipating the Declaration of Independence,\n       <a href="/wiki/Patriot_(American_Revolution)" title="Patriot (American Revolution)">\n        Patriot\n       </a>\n       leaders Thomas McKean and\n       <a href="/wiki/Caesar_Rodney" title="Caesar Rodney">\n        Caesar Rodney\n       </a>\n       convinced the Colonial Assembly to declare itself separated from British and Pennsylvania rule on June 15, 1776. The person best representing Delaware\'s majority,\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/George_Read_(signer)" title="George Read (signer)">\n        George Read\n       </a>\n       , could not bring himself to vote for a Declaration of Independence. Only the dramatic overnight ride of Caesar Rodney gave the delegation the votes needed to cast Delaware\'s vote for independence.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Initially led by\n       <a href="/wiki/John_Haslet" title="John Haslet">\n        John Haslet\n       </a>\n       , Delaware provided one of the premier regiments in the\n       <a href="/wiki/Continental_Army" title="Continental Army">\n        Continental Army\n       </a>\n       , known as the "Delaware Blues" and nicknamed the "\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Blue_Hen_Chicken" title="Blue Hen Chicken">\n        Blue Hen\'s Chicks\n       </a>\n       ." In August 1777\n       <a href="/wiki/William_Howe,_5th_Viscount_Howe" title="William Howe, 5th Viscount Howe">\n        General Sir William Howe\n       </a>\n       led a British army through Delaware on his way to a victory at the\n       <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Brandywine" title="Battle of Brandywine">\n        Battle of Brandywine\n       </a>\n       and capture of the city of Philadelphia. The only real engagement on Delaware soil was the\n       <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Cooch%27s_Bridge" title="Battle of Cooch\'s Bridge">\n        Battle of Cooch\'s Bridge\n       </a>\n       , fought on September 3, 1777, at\n       <a href="/wiki/Cooch%27s_Bridge" title="Cooch\'s Bridge">\n        Cooch\'s Bridge\n       </a>\n       in New Castle County.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Following the Battle of Brandywine, Wilmington was occupied by the British, and\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Governor_of_Delaware" title="Governor of Delaware">\n        State President\n       </a>\n       <a href="/wiki/John_McKinly" title="John McKinly">\n        John McKinly\n       </a>\n       was taken prisoner. The British remained in control of the Delaware River for much of the rest of the war, disrupting commerce and providing encouragement to an active\n       <a href="/wiki/Loyalist_(American_Revolution)" title="Loyalist (American Revolution)">\n        Loyalist\n       </a>\n       portion of the population, particularly in Sussex County. Because the British promised slaves of rebels freedom for fighting with them, escaped slaves flocked north to join their lines.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25">\n        <a href="#cite_note-25">\n         [23]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Following the\n       <a href="/wiki/American_Revolution" title="American Revolution">\n        American Revolution\n       </a>\n       , statesmen from Delaware were among the leading proponents of a strong central United States with equal representation for each state.\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Slavery_and_race">\n        Slavery and race\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <table class="plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Refimprove" role="presentation">\n       <tr>\n        <td class="mbox-image">\n         <div style="width:52px">\n          <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg">\n           <img alt="" data-file-height="399" data-file-width="512" height="39" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/50px-Question_book-new.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/75px-Question_book-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/100px-Question_book-new.svg.png 2x" width="50"/>\n          </a>\n         </div>\n        </td>\n        <td class="mbox-text">\n         <div class="mbox-text-span">\n          This section\n          <b>\n           needs additional citations for\n           <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">\n            verification\n           </a>\n          </b>\n          .\n          <span class="hide-when-compact">\n           Please help\n           <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Delaware&amp;action=edit">\n            improve this article\n           </a>\n           by\n           <a href="/wiki/Help:Introduction_to_referencing_with_Wiki_Markup/1" title="Help:Introduction to referencing with Wiki Markup/1">\n            adding citations to reliable sources\n           </a>\n           . Unsourced material may be challenged and removed.\n          </span>\n          <small>\n           <i>\n            (April 2014)\n           </i>\n          </small>\n          <small class="hide-when-compact">\n           <i>\n            (\n            <a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">\n             Learn how and when to remove this template message\n            </a>\n            )\n           </i>\n          </small>\n         </div>\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n      </table>\n      <p>\n       Many colonial settlers came to Delaware from Maryland and Virginia, which had been experiencing a population boom. The economies of these colonies were chiefly based on tobacco culture and were increasingly dependent on slave labor for its intensive cultivation. Most of the English colonists arrived as\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Indentured_servant" title="Indentured servant">\n        indentured servants\n       </a>\n       , under contracts to work as laborers for a fixed period to pay for their passage. In the early years the line between indentured servants and African\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Slave" title="Slave">\n        slaves\n       </a>\n       or laborers was fluid, and the working classes often lived closely together. Most of the free African-American families in Delaware before the Revolution had migrated from Maryland to find more affordable land. They were descendants chiefly of relationships or marriages between white servant women and enslaved, servant or free African or African-American men.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26">\n        <a href="#cite_note-26">\n         [24]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       As the flow of indentured laborers to the colony decreased with improving economic conditions in England, more slaves were imported for labor and the caste lines hardened.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       At the end of the colonial period, the number of enslaved people in Delaware began to decline. Shifts in the agriculture economy from tobacco to mixed farming created less need for slaves\' labor. Local\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Methodist" title="Methodist">\n        Methodists\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Quaker" title="Quaker">\n        Quakers\n       </a>\n       encouraged slaveholders to free their slaves following the American Revolution, and many did so in a surge of individual manumissions for idealistic reasons. By 1810 three-quarters of all blacks in Delaware were free. When John Dickinson freed his slaves in 1777, he was Delaware\'s largest slave owner with 37 slaves. By 1860, the largest slaveholder owned 16 slaves.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKolchin199478.2C_81.E2.80.9382_27-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKolchin199478.2C_81.E2.80.9382-27">\n         [25]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Although attempts to abolish slavery failed by narrow margins in the legislature, in practical terms, the state had mostly ended the practice. By the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/United_States_Census,_1860" title="United States Census, 1860">\n        1860 census\n       </a>\n       on the verge of the\n       <a href="/wiki/American_Civil_War" title="American Civil War">\n        Civil War\n       </a>\n       , 91.7% of the black population were free;\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKolchin199481.E2.80.9382_28-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKolchin199481.E2.80.9382-28">\n         [26]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       1,798 were slaves, as compared to 19,829 "free colored persons".\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29">\n        <a href="#cite_note-29">\n         [27]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The independent black denomination was chartered by freed slave\n       <a href="/wiki/Peter_Spencer_(religious_leader)" title="Peter Spencer (religious leader)">\n        Peter Spencer\n       </a>\n       in 1813 as the "\n       <a href="/wiki/Spencer_Churches" title="Spencer Churches">\n        Union Church of Africans\n       </a>\n       ". This followed the 1793 establishment of the African Methodist Episcopal Church in Philadelphia, which had ties to the Methodist Episcopal Church until 1816. Spencer built a church in Wilmington for the new denomination.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30">\n        <a href="#cite_note-30">\n         [28]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       This was renamed the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/African_Union_First_Colored_Methodist_Protestant_Church_and_Connection" title="African Union First Colored Methodist Protestant Church and Connection">\n        African Union First Colored Methodist Protestant Church and Connection\n       </a>\n       , more commonly known as the\n       <a href="/wiki/A.U.M.P._Church" title="A.U.M.P. Church">\n        A.U.M.P. Church\n       </a>\n       . Begun by Spencer in 1814, the annual gathering of the\n       <a href="/wiki/Big_August_Quarterly" title="Big August Quarterly">\n        Big August Quarterly\n       </a>\n       still draws people together in a religious and cultural festival, the oldest such cultural festival in the nation.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Delaware voted against secession on January 3, 1861, and so remained in the Union. While most Delaware citizens who fought in the war served in the regiments of the state, some served in companies on the Confederate side in\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Maryland_Civil_War_Confederate_units" title="Maryland Civil War Confederate units">\n        Maryland\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/List_of_Virginia_Civil_War_units" title="List of Virginia Civil War units">\n        Virginia\n       </a>\n       Regiments. Delaware is notable for being the only slave state from which no Confederate regiments or militia groups were assembled. Delaware essentially freed the few slaves that were still in bondage shortly after the Civil War, but rejected the\n       <a href="/wiki/Thirteenth_Amendment_to_the_United_States_Constitution" title="Thirteenth Amendment to the United States Constitution">\n        13th\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Fourteenth_Amendment_to_the_United_States_Constitution" title="Fourteenth Amendment to the United States Constitution">\n        14th\n       </a>\n       , and\n       <a href="/wiki/Fifteenth_Amendment_to_the_United_States_Constitution" title="Fifteenth Amendment to the United States Constitution">\n        15th\n       </a>\n       Amendments to the Constitution; the 13th Amendment was rejected on February 8, 1865, the 14th Amendment was rejected on February 8, 1867, and the 15th Amendment was rejected on March 18, 1869. Delaware officially ratified the 13th, 14th, and 15th amendments on February 12, 1901.\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Demographics">\n        Demographics\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       See also:\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Largest_municipalities_in_Delaware" title="Largest municipalities in Delaware">\n        Largest municipalities in Delaware\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Delaware_population_map.png">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="600" data-file-width="600" height="220" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c7/Delaware_population_map.png/220px-Delaware_population_map.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c7/Delaware_population_map.png/330px-Delaware_population_map.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c7/Delaware_population_map.png/440px-Delaware_population_map.png 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Delaware_population_map.png" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         Delaware population density map\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <table class="toccolours" style="border-spacing: 1px; text-align: center;">\n         6.0%\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n       <tr>\n        <td colspan="4" style="border-top:1px solid black; font-size:85%; text-align:center">\n         Source: 1910\xe2\x80\x932010\n         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31">\n          <a href="#cite_note-31">\n           [29]\n          </a>\n         </sup>\n         <br/>\n         2015 estimate\n         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PopEstUS_32-0">\n          <a href="#cite_note-PopEstUS-32">\n           [30]\n          </a>\n         </sup>\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n      </table>\n      <p>\n       The\n       <a href="/wiki/United_States_Census_Bureau" title="United States Census Bureau">\n        United States Census Bureau\n       </a>\n       estimates that the population of Delaware was 952,065 people on July 1, 2016, a 6.0% increase since the\n       <a href="/wiki/2010_United_States_Census" title="2010 United States Census">\n        2010 United States Census\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PopEstUS_32-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-PopEstUS-32">\n         [30]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Ancestry">\n        Ancestry\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <p>\n       According to the 2010 United States Census, Delaware had a population of 897,934 people. The racial composition of the state was:\n      </p>\n      <ul>\n       <li>\n        68.9%\n        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/White_American" title="White American">\n         White of any race made up 8.2% of the population.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33">\n        <a href="#cite_note-33">\n         [31]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <table </td>\n        <td>\n         1.1%\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         2.0%\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         3.4%\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n       <tr>\n        <td>\n         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Multiracial_American" title="Multiracial American">\n          Two or more races\n         </a>\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         \xe2\x80\x93\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         1.7%\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         2.7%\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n      </table>\n      <p>\n       Delaware is the sixth most densely populated state, with a population density of 442.6 people per square mile, 356.4 per square mile more than the national average, and ranking 45th in population. Delaware is one of five states that do not have a single city with a population over 100,000 as of the 2010 census, the other four being West Virginia, Vermont, Maine and Wyoming.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Census_37-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Census-37">\n         [35]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The\n       <a href="/wiki/Center_of_population" title="Center of population">\n        center of population\n       </a>\n       of Delaware is located in New Castle County, in the town of\n       <a href="/wiki/Townsend,_Delaware" title="Townsend, Delaware">\n        Townsend\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cenpopcenter_38-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-cenpopcenter-38">\n         [36]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       As of 2011, 49.7% of Delaware\'s population younger than one year of age belonged to minority groups (i.e., did not have two parents of non-Hispanic white ancestry).\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39">\n        <a href="#cite_note-39">\n         [37]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       In 2000 approximately 19% of the population were African-American and 5% of the population is Hispanic (mostly of Puerto Rican or Mexican ancestry).\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40">\n        <a href="#cite_note-40">\n         [38]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The largest European ancestry groups in Delaware are, according to 2012 Census Bureau estimates:\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41">\n        <a href="#cite_note-41">\n         [39]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">\n        [\n        <i>\n         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">\n          <span title="The material near this tag failed verification of its source citation(s). </td>\n        <td>\n         <b>\n          11,166\n         </b>\n         (100%)\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n      </table>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Languages">\n        Languages\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <p>\n       As of 2000 91% of Delaware residents age 5 and older speak only English at home; 5% speak Spanish. French is the third most spoken language at 0.7%, followed by Chinese at 0.5% and German at 0.5%.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Legislation had been proposed in both the House and the Senate in Delaware to designate English as the\n       <a href="/wiki/Languages_of_the_United_States" title="Languages of the United States">\n        official language\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45">\n        <a href="#cite_note-45">\n         [43]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46">\n        <a href="#cite_note-46">\n         [44]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Neither bill was passed in the legislature.\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Religion">\n        Religion\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="barbox tright" style="overflow-x: auto;">\n       <div style="border:1px solid silver; font-size:88%; padding:0.4em; width:auto; background: white;">\n        <table style="border-collapse:collapse; width:100%;">\n         <tr style="background:#ddd">\n          <th colspan="5">\n           Religion in Delaware (2014)\n           <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pew2014_47-0">\n            <a href="#cite_note-pew2014-47">\n             [45]\n            </a>\n           </sup>\n          </th>\n         </tr>\n         <tr style="font-size:88%; border-left: solid 1px silver; border-right: solid 1px silver;">\n           <div style="background:pink; width:1%; overflow: hidden;">\n           </div>\n          </td>\n          <td colspan="2" style="padding-left: 0.4em; padding-right: 0.4em; text-align: right;">\n           1%\n          </td>\n         </tr>\n        </table>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       As of the year 2010, The Association of Religion Data Archives\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-www.thearda.com_48-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-www.thearda.com-48">\n         [46]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       reported that the three largest denominational groups in Delaware by number of adherents are the\n       <a href="/wiki/Catholic_Church" title="Catholic Church">\n        Catholic Church\n       </a>\n       at 182,532 adherents, the\n       <a href="/wiki/United_Methodist_Church" title="United Methodist Church">\n        United Methodist Church\n       </a>\n       with 53,656 members reported, and non-denominational\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Evangelical_Protestant" title="Evangelical Protestant">\n        Evangelical Protestant\n       </a>\n       with 22,973 adherents reported. The religious body with the largest number of congregations is the United Methodist Church (with 158 congregations) followed by non-denominational Evangelical Protestant (with 106 congregations), then the Catholic Church (with 45 congregations).\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The\n       <a href="/wiki/Roman_Catholic_Diocese_of_Wilmington" title="Roman Catholic Diocese of Wilmington">\n        Roman Catholic Diocese of Wilmington\n       </a>\n       and the\n       <a href="/wiki/Episcopal_Diocese_of_Delaware" title="Episcopal Diocese of Delaware">\n        Episcopal Diocese of Delaware\n       </a>\n       oversee the parishes within their denominations. The A.U.M.P. Church, the oldest African-American denomination in the nation, was founded in Wilmington. It still has a substantial presence in the state. Reflecting new immigrant populations, an\n       <a href="/wiki/Mosque" title="Mosque">\n        Islamic mosque\n       </a>\n       has been built in the\n       <a href="/wiki/Ogletown,_Delaware" title="Ogletown, Delaware">\n        Ogletown\n       </a>\n       area, and a\n       <a href="/wiki/Hindu_temple" title="Hindu temple">\n        Hindu temple\n       </a>\n       in\n       <a href="/wiki/Hockessin,_Delaware" title="Hockessin, Delaware">\n        Hockessin\n       </a>\n       .\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Delaware is home to an\n       <a href="/wiki/Amish" title="Amish">\n        Amish\n       </a>\n       community that resides to the west of\n       <a href="/wiki/Dover,_Delaware" title="Dover, Delaware">\n        Dover\n       </a>\n       in\n       <a href="/wiki/Kent_County,_Delaware" title="Kent County, Delaware">\n        Kent County\n       </a>\n       , consisting of 9 church districts and between 1,200 and 1,500 people. The Amish first settled in Kent County in 1915. In recent years, increasing development has led to the decline in the number of Amish living in the community.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-visitdoveramish_49-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-visitdoveramish-49">\n         [47]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-amishamerica_50-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-amishamerica-50">\n         [48]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       A 2012 survey of religious attitudes in the United States found that 34% of Delaware residents considered themselves "moderately religious," 33% "very religious," and 33% as "non-religious."\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-51">\n        <a href="#cite_note-51">\n         [49]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Sexual_orientation">\n        Sexual orientation\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <p>\n       A 2012 Gallup poll found that Delaware\'s proportion of lesbian, gay, bisexual, and transgender adults stood at 3.4 percent of the population. This constitutes a total LGBT adult population estimate of 23,698 people. The number of same-sex couple households in 2010 stood at 2,646. This grew by 41.65% from a decade earlier.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-52">\n        <a href="#cite_note-52">\n         [50]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">\n        [\n        <i>\n         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">\n          <span title="The citation is not specific enough to facilitate source verification (November 2013)">\n           not specific enough to verify\n          </span>\n         </a>\n        </i>\n        ]\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-53">\n        <a href="#cite_note-53">\n         [51]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       On July 1, 2013, same-sex marriage was legalized, and all civil unions would be converted into marriages.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-54">\n        <a href="#cite_note-54">\n         [52]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">\n        [\n        <i>\n         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">\n          <span title="The citation is not specific enough to facilitate source verification (November 2013)">\n           not specific enough to verify\n          </span>\n         </a>\n        </i>\n        ]\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n
