</div>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Affluence">\n        Affluence\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <table class="wikitable" style="float: right; margin: 10px">\n       <caption>\n        Average sale price for new &amp; existing homes (in US$)\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-er2011_55-0">\n         <a href="#cite_note-er2011-55">\n          [53]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n       </caption>\n       <tr>\n        <th>\n         DE County\n        </th>\n        <th>\n         March 2010\n        </th>\n        <th>\n         March 2011\n        </th>\n       </tr>\n       <tr>\n        <td>\n         New Castle\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         229,000\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         216,000\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n       <tr>\n        <td>\n         Sussex\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         323,000\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         296,000\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n       <tr>\n        <td>\n         Kent\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         186,000\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         178,000\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n      </table>\n      <p>\n       According to a 2013 study by Phoenix Marketing International, Delaware had the ninth-largest number of millionaires per capita in the United States, with a ratio of 6.20 percent.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-frank2014_56-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-frank2014-56">\n         [54]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Agriculture">\n        Agriculture\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Peach_delaware.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="401" data-file-width="600" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2d/Peach_delaware.jpg/220px-Peach_delaware.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2d/Peach_delaware.jpg/330px-Peach_delaware.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2d/Peach_delaware.jpg/440px-Peach_delaware.jpg 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Peach_delaware.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         "Picking Peaches in Delaware" from an 1878 issue of\n         <a href="/wiki/Harper%27s_Weekly" title="Harper\'s Weekly">\n          Harper\'s Weekly\n         </a>\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       Delaware\'s agricultural output consists of poultry, nursery stock,\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Soybeans" title="Soybeans">\n        soybeans\n       </a>\n       , dairy products and\n       <a href="/wiki/Maize" title="Maize">\n        corn\n       </a>\n       .\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Industries">\n        Industries\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <p>\n       As of October 2015, the state\'s unemployment rate was 5.1%.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ktdidit_57-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-ktdidit-57">\n         [55]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The state\'s largest employers are:\n       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">\n        [\n        <i>\n         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Accuracy_dispute#Disputed_statement" title="Wikipedia:Accuracy dispute">\n          <span title="The material near this tag is possibly inaccurate or nonfactual. (March 2012)">\n           dubious\n          </span>\n         </a>\n         <span class="metadata">\n          \xe2\x80\x93\n          <a href="/wiki/Talk:Delaware#largest_employers" title="Talk:Delaware">\n           discuss\n          </a>\n         </span>\n        </i>\n        ]\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <ul>\n       <li>\n        government (State of Delaware, New Castle County)\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        education (\n        <a href="/wiki/University_of_Delaware" title="University of Delaware">\n         University of Delaware\n        </a>\n        ,\n        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Delaware_Technical_%26_Community_College" title="Delaware Technical &amp; Community College">\n         Delaware Technical &amp; Community College\n        </a>\n        )\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        banking (\n        <a href="/wiki/Bank_of_America" title="Bank of America">\n         Bank of America\n        </a>\n        ,\n        <a href="/wiki/M%26T_Bank" title="M&amp;T Bank">\n         M&amp;T Bank\n        </a>\n        ,\n        <a href="/wiki/JPMorgan_Chase" title="JPMorgan Chase">\n         JPMorgan Chase\n        </a>\n        ,\n        <a href="/wiki/Citigroup" title="Citigroup">\n         Citigroup\n        </a>\n        ,\n        <a href="/wiki/Deutsche_Bank" title="Deutsche Bank">\n         Deutsche Bank\n        </a>\n        )\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        chemical, pharmaceutical, technology (\n        <a href="/wiki/DuPont" title="DuPont">\n         E.I. du Pont de Nemours &amp; Co.\n        </a>\n        ,\n        <a href="/wiki/AstraZeneca" title="AstraZeneca">\n         AstraZeneca\n        </a>\n        ,\n        <a href="/wiki/Syngenta" title="Syngenta">\n         Syngenta\n        </a>\n        ,\n        <a href="/wiki/Agilent_Technologies" title="Agilent Technologies">\n         Agilent Technologies\n        </a>\n        )\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        healthcare (\n        <a href="/wiki/Christiana_Care_Health_System" title="Christiana Care Health System">\n         Christiana Care Health System\n        </a>\n        , Bayhealth Medical Center,\n        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Alfred_I._duPont_Hospital_for_Children" title="Alfred I. duPont Hospital for Children">\n         Alfred I. duPont Hospital for Children\n        </a>\n        )\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        farming, specifically chicken farming in Sussex County (\n        <a href="/wiki/Perdue_Farms" title="Perdue Farms">\n         Perdue Farms\n        </a>\n        , Mountaire Farms,\n        <a href="/wiki/Allen_Family_Foods" title="Allen Family Foods">\n         Allen Family Foods\n        </a>\n        )\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        retail (\n        <a href="/wiki/Walmart" title="Walmart">\n         Walmart\n        </a>\n        ,\n        <a href="/wiki/Walgreens" title="Walgreens">\n         Walgreens\n        </a>\n        ,\n        <a href="/wiki/Acme_Markets" title="Acme Markets">\n         Acme Markets\n        </a>\n        )\n       </li>\n      </ul>\n      <p>\n       <a href="/wiki/Dover_Air_Force_Base" title="Dover Air Force Base">\n        Dover Air Force Base\n       </a>\n       , located next to the state capital of\n       <a href="/wiki/Dover,_Delaware" title="Dover, Delaware">\n        Dover\n       </a>\n       , is one of the largest Air Force bases in the country and is a major employer in Delaware. In addition to its other responsibilities in the\n       <a href="/wiki/Air_Mobility_Command" title="Air Mobility Command">\n        United States Air Force Air Mobility Command\n       </a>\n       , this air base serves as the entry point and\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mortuary" title="Mortuary">\n        mortuary\n       </a>\n       for American military personnel and some U.S. government civilians who die overseas.\n      </p>\n      <h4>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Recent_departures">\n        Recent departures\n       </span>\n      </h4>\n      <table class="plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-POV" role="presentation">\n       <tr>\n        <td class="mbox-image">\n         <div style="width:52px">\n          <img alt="Unbalanced scales.svg" data-file-height="354" data-file-width="400" height="40" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fe/Unbalanced_scales.svg/45px-Unbalanced_scales.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fe/Unbalanced_scales.svg/68px-Unbalanced_scales.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fe/Unbalanced_scales.svg/90px-Unbalanced_scales.svg.png 2x" width="45"/>\n         </div>\n        </td>\n        <td class="mbox-text">\n         <div class="mbox-text-span">\n          The\n          <b>\n           <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Neutral_point_of_view" title="Wikipedia:Neutral point of view">\n            neutrality\n           </a>\n           of this section is\n           <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:NPOV_dispute" title="Wikipedia:NPOV dispute">\n            disputed\n           </a>\n          </b>\n          .\n          <span class="hide-when-compact">\n           Relevant discussion may be found on the\n           <a href="/wiki/Talk:Delaware#.23" title="Talk:Delaware">\n            talk page\n           </a>\n           . Please do not remove this message until\n           <a href="/wiki/Template:POV#When_to_remove" title="Template:POV">\n            conditions to do so are met\n           </a>\n           .\n          </span>\n          <small>\n           <i>\n            (July 2016)\n           </i>\n          </small>\n          <small class="hide-when-compact">\n           <i>\n            (\n            <a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">\n             Learn how and when to remove this template message\n            </a>\n            )\n           </i>\n          </small>\n         </div>\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n      </table>\n      <p>\n       The recent merger of\n       <a href="/wiki/DuPont" title="DuPont">\n        E.I. du Pont de Nemours &amp; Co.\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Dow_Chemical_Company" title="Dow Chemical Company">\n        Dow Chemical Company\n       </a>\n       (pending likely federal regulatory approval) has caused many to question the viability of DuPont in Delaware, which employs over 8,000 as the state\'s second largest private employer, as well as the stability of the state\'s economic future.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-58">\n        <a href="#cite_note-58">\n         [56]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-59">\n        <a href="#cite_note-59">\n         [57]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-60">\n        <a href="#cite_note-60">\n         [58]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-61">\n        <a href="#cite_note-61">\n         [59]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       In late 2015, DuPont announced that 1,700 employees, nearly a third of its footprint in Delaware, would be laid off in early 2016.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-62">\n        <a href="#cite_note-62">\n         [60]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Since the mid-2000s, Delaware has suffered an onslaught of economic downfalls affecting stable middle class jobs including: the departure of the state\'s automotive manufacturing industry (\n       <a href="/wiki/General_Motors" title="General Motors">\n        General Motors\n       </a>\n       <a href="/wiki/Wilmington_Assembly" title="Wilmington Assembly">\n        Wilmington Assembly\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Chrysler" title="Chrysler">\n        Chrysler\n       </a>\n       <a href="/wiki/Newark_Assembly" title="Newark Assembly">\n        Newark Assembly\n       </a>\n       ), the corporate buyout of a major bank holding company (\n       <a href="/wiki/MBNA" title="MBNA">\n        MBNA\n       </a>\n       ), the departure of the state\'s steel industry (\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Evraz_Claymont_Steel" title="Evraz Claymont Steel">\n        Evraz Claymont Steel\n       </a>\n       ), the bankruptcy of a fiber mill (National Vulcanized Fibre),\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-63">\n        <a href="#cite_note-63">\n         [61]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       and the diminishing presence of\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Astra_Zeneca" title="Astra Zeneca">\n        Astra Zeneca\n       </a>\n       in Wilmington.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-64">\n        <a href="#cite_note-64">\n         [62]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-65">\n        <a href="#cite_note-65">\n         [63]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Incorporation_in_Delaware">\n        Incorporation in Delaware\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       Main article:\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Delaware_corporation" title="Delaware corporation">\n        Delaware corporation\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       More than 50% of all U.S. publicly traded companies and 63% of the\n       <a href="/wiki/Fortune_500" title="Fortune 500">\n        Fortune 500\n       </a>\n       are\n       <a href="/wiki/Incorporation_(business)" title="Incorporation (business)">\n        incorporated\n       </a>\n       in Delaware.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-66">\n        <a href="#cite_note-66">\n         [64]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The state\'s attractiveness as a\n       <a href="/wiki/Corporate_haven" title="Corporate haven">\n        corporate haven\n       </a>\n       is largely because of its business-friendly\n       <a href="/wiki/Delaware_General_Corporation_Law" title="Delaware General Corporation Law">\n        corporation law\n       </a>\n       .\n       <a href="/wiki/Franchise_tax" title="Franchise tax">\n        Franchise taxes\n       </a>\n       on Delaware corporations supply about one-fifth of its state revenue.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-DEFiscalNotebook_67-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-DEFiscalNotebook-67">\n         [65]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Although "USA (Delaware)" ranked as the world\'s most opaque jurisdiction on the\n       <a href="/wiki/Tax_Justice_Network" title="Tax Justice Network">\n        Tax Justice Network\n       </a>\n       \'s 2009 Financial Secrecy Index,\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-68">\n        <a href="#cite_note-68">\n         [66]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       the same group\'s 2011 Index ranks the USA fifth and does not specify Delaware.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-69">\n        <a href="#cite_note-69">\n         [67]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       In Delaware, there are more than a million registered corporations,\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-70">\n        <a href="#cite_note-70">\n         [68]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       meaning there are more corporations than people.\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Food_and_drink">\n        Food and drink\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <p>\n       <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wikisource.org/wiki/Delaware_Code/Title_4/Chapter_7" title="wikisource:Delaware Code/Title 4/Chapter 7">\n        Title 4, chapter 7 of the Delaware Code\n       </a>\n       stipulates that alcoholic liquor only be sold in specifically licensed establishments, and only between 9:00\xc2\xa0am and 1:00\xc2\xa0am.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-delcode4-8_71-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-delcode4-8-71">\n         [69]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Until 2003, Delaware was among the several states enforcing\n       <a href="/wiki/Blue_law" title="Blue law">\n        blue laws\n       </a>\n       and banned the sale of liquor on Sunday.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nathans2011_72-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-nathans2011-72">\n         [70]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Transportation">\n        Transportation\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:DE_2005.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="100" data-file-width="200" height="100" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/8/83/DE_2005.jpg" width="200"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:DE_2005.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         The current\n         <a href="/wiki/Vehicle_registration_plates_of_Delaware" title="Vehicle registration plates of Delaware">\n          state license plate\n         </a>\n         design was introduced in 1959, making it the longest-running license plate design in United States history.\n         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-73">\n          <a href="#cite_note-73">\n           [71]\n          </a>\n         </sup>\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       The transportation system in Delaware is under the governance and supervision of the\n       <a href="/wiki/Delaware_Department_of_Transportation" title="Delaware Department of Transportation">\n        Delaware Department of Transportation\n       </a>\n       , also known as "DelDOT".\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-74">\n        <a href="#cite_note-74">\n         [72]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-75">\n        <a href="#cite_note-75">\n         [73]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Funding for DelDOT projects is drawn, in part, from the Delaware Transportation Trust Fund, established in 1987 to help stabilize transportation funding; the availability of the Trust led to a gradual separation of DelDOT operations from other Delaware state operations.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-montgomery2012nj_76-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-montgomery2012nj-76">\n         [74]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       DelDOT manages programs such as a Delaware\n       <a href="/wiki/Adopt-a-Highway" title="Adopt-a-Highway">\n        Adopt-a-Highway\n       </a>\n       program, major road route snow removal, traffic control infrastructure (signs and signals), toll road management, Delaware\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Division_of_Motor_Vehicles" title="Division of Motor Vehicles">\n        Division of Motor Vehicles\n       </a>\n       , the Delaware Transit Corporation (branded as "\n       <a href="/wiki/DART_First_State" title="DART First State">\n        DART First State\n       </a>\n       ", the state government public transportation organization), among others. In 2009, DelDOT maintained 13,507 lane miles of roads, totaling 89 percent of the state\'s public roadway system; the remaining public road miles are under the supervision of individual municipalities. This far exceeds the United States national average of 20 percent for state department of transportation maintenance responsibility.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-deldotfactbook_77-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-deldotfactbook-77">\n         [75]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The "DART First State" public transportation system was named "Most Outstanding Public Transportation System" in 2003 by the\n       <a href="/wiki/American_Public_Transportation_Association" title="American Public Transportation Association">\n        American Public Transportation Association\n       </a>\n       . Coverage of the system is broad within northern New Castle County with close association to major highways in Kent and Sussex counties. The system includes bus, subsidized passenger rail operated by Philadelphia transit agency SEPTA, and subsidized taxi and\n       <a href="/wiki/Paratransit" title="Paratransit">\n        paratransit\n       </a>\n       modes. The paratransit system, consisting of a statewide door-to-door bus service for the elderly and disabled, has been described by a Delaware state report as "the most generous paratransit system in the United States."\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-montgomery2012nj_76-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-montgomery2012nj-76">\n         [74]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       As of 2012\n       <sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;">\n        <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Delaware&amp;action=edit">\n         [update]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       , fees for the paratransit service have not changed since 1988.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-montgomery2012nj_76-2">\n        <a href="#cite_note-montgomery2012nj-76">\n         [74]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Roads">\n        Roads\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       Further information:\n       <a href="/wiki/Delaware_State_Route_System" title="Delaware State Route System">\n        Delaware State Route System\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:DE_1_near_canal.JPG">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1712" data-file-width="2288" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4b/DE_1_near_canal.JPG/220px-DE_1_near_canal.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4b/DE_1_near_canal.JPG/330px-DE_1_near_canal.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4b/DE_1_near_canal.JPG/440px-DE_1_near_canal.JPG 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:DE_1_near_canal.JPG" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         <a href="/wiki/Delaware_Route_1" title="Delaware Route 1">\n          Delaware Route\xc2\xa01\n         </a>\n         (DE\xc2\xa01), a partial\n         <a href="/wiki/Toll_road" title="Toll road">\n          toll road\n         </a>\n         linking\n         <a href="/wiki/Fenwick_Island,_Delaware" title="Fenwick Island, Delaware">\n          Fenwick Island\n         </a>\n         and\n         <a href="/wiki/Wilmington,_Delaware" title="Wilmington, Delaware">\n          Wilmington\n         </a>\n         .\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       One major branch of the U.S.\n       <a href="/wiki/Interstate_Highway_System" title="Interstate Highway System">\n        Interstate Highway System\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Interstate_95_in_Delaware" title="Interstate 95 in Delaware">\n        Interstate\xc2\xa095\n       </a>\n       (I-95), crosses Delaware southwest-to-northeast across New Castle County. In addition to I-95, there are six\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/U.S._Highway_System" title="U.S. Highway System">\n        U.S. highways\n       </a>\n       that serve Delaware:\n       <a href="/wiki/U.S._Route_9_in_Delaware" title="U.S. Route 9 in Delaware">\n        U.S. Route\xc2\xa09\n       </a>\n       (US\xc2\xa09),\n       <a href="/wiki/U.S._Route_13_in_Delaware" title="U.S. Route 13 in Delaware">\n        US\xc2\xa013\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/U.S._Route_40_in_Delaware" title="U.S. Route 40 in Delaware">\n        US\xc2\xa040\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/U.S._Route_113_in_Delaware" title="U.S. Route 113 in Delaware">\n        US\xc2\xa0113\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/U.S._Route_202_in_Delaware" title="U.S. Route 202 in Delaware">\n        US\xc2\xa0202\n       </a>\n       , and\n       <a href="/wiki/U.S._Route_301_in_Delaware" title="U.S. Route 301 in Delaware">\n        US\xc2\xa0301\n       </a>\n       . There are also several state highways that cross the state of Delaware; a few of them include\n       <a href="/wiki/Delaware_Route_1" title="Delaware Route 1">\n        Delaware Route\xc2\xa01\n       </a>\n       (DE\xc2\xa01),\n       <a href="/wiki/Delaware_Route_9" title="Delaware Route 9">\n        DE\xc2\xa09\n       </a>\n       , and\n       <a href="/wiki/Delaware_Route_404" title="Delaware Route 404">\n        DE\xc2\xa0404\n       </a>\n       . US\xc2\xa013 and DE\xc2\xa01 are primary north-south highways connecting Wilmington and Pennsylvania with Maryland, with DE\xc2\xa01 serving as the main route between Wilmington and the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Delaware_beaches" title="Delaware beaches">\n        Delaware beaches\n       </a>\n       . DE\xc2\xa09 is a north-south highway connecting Dover and Wilmington via a scenic route along the\n       <a href="/wiki/Delaware_Bay" title="Delaware Bay">\n        Delaware Bay\n       </a>\n       . US\xc2\xa040, is a primary east-west route, connecting Maryland with New Jersey. DE\xc2\xa0404 is another primary east-west highway connecting the\n       <a href="/wiki/Chesapeake_Bay_Bridge" title="Chesapeake Bay Bridge">\n        Chesapeake Bay Bridge\n       </a>\n       in Maryland with the Delaware beaches. The state also operates two toll highways, the\n       <a href="/wiki/Delaware_Turnpike" title="Delaware Turnpike">\n        Delaware Turnpike\n       </a>\n       , which is I-95, between Maryland and New Castle and the Korean War Veterans Memorial Highway, which is DE\xc2\xa01, between Wilmington and Dover.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       A bicycle route,\n       <a href="/wiki/Delaware_Bicycle_Route_1" title="Delaware Bicycle Route 1">\n        Delaware Bicycle Route\xc2\xa01\n       </a>\n       , spans the north-south length of the state from the Maryland border in\n       <a href="/wiki/Fenwick_Island,_Delaware" title="Fenwick Island, Delaware">\n        Fenwick Island\n       </a>\n       to the Pennsylvania border north of\n       <a href="/wiki/Montchanin,_Delaware" title="Montchanin, Delaware">\n        Montchanin\n       </a>\n       . It is the first of several signed bike routes planned in Delaware.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-78">\n        <a href="#cite_note-78">\n         [76]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Delaware has around 1,450 bridges, 95 percent of which are under the supervision of DelDOT. About 30 percent of all Delaware bridges were built before 1950, and about 60 percent of the number are included in the\n       <a href="/wiki/National_Bridge_Inventory" title="National Bridge Inventory">\n        National Bridge Inventory\n       </a>\n       . Some bridges not under DelDOT supervision includes the four bridges on the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Chesapeake_and_Delaware_Canal" title="Chesapeake and Delaware Canal">\n        Chesapeake and Delaware Canal\n       </a>\n       , which are under the jurisdiction of the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/U.S._Army_Corps_of_Engineers" title="U.S. Army Corps of Engineers">\n        U.S. Army Corps of Engineers\n       </a>\n       , and the\n       <a href="/wiki/Delaware_Memorial_Bridge" title="Delaware Memorial Bridge">\n        Delaware Memorial Bridge\n       </a>\n       , which is under the bi-state\n       <a href="/wiki/Delaware_River_and_Bay_Authority" title="Delaware River and Bay Authority">\n        Delaware River and Bay Authority\n       </a>\n       .\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       It has been noted that the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tar_and_chip" title="Tar and chip">\n        tar and chip\n       </a>\n       composition of secondary roads in Sussex County make them more prone to\n       <a href="/wiki/Road_surface#Surface_deterioration" title="Road surface">\n        deterioration\n       </a>\n       than\n       <a href="/wiki/Asphalt_concrete" title="Asphalt concrete">\n        asphalt\n       </a>\n       roadways found in almost the rest of the state.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nj20110417_79-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-nj20110417-79">\n         [77]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Among these roads, Sussex (county road) 236 is among the most problematic.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nj20110417_79-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-nj20110417-79">\n         [77]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Ferries">\n        Ferries\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:MVDelaware.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="900" data-file-width="1200" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/ff/MVDelaware.jpg/220px-MVDelaware.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/ff/MVDelaware.jpg/330px-MVDelaware.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/ff/MVDelaware.jpg/440px-MVDelaware.jpg 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:MVDelaware.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         Cape May-Lewes Ferry\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       There are three ferries that operate in the state of Delaware:\n      </p>\n      <ul>\n       <li>\n        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cape_May-Lewes_Ferry" title="Cape May-Lewes Ferry">\n         Cape May-Lewes Ferry\n        </a>\n        crosses the mouth of the Delaware Bay between Lewes, Delaware and\n        <a href="/wiki/Cape_May,_New_Jersey" title="Cape May, New Jersey">\n         Cape May, New Jersey\n        </a>\n        .\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        <a href="/wiki/Woodland_Ferry" title="Woodland Ferry">\n         Woodland Ferry\n        </a>\n        is a cable ferry that crosses the\n        <a href="/wiki/Nanticoke_River" title="Nanticoke River">\n         Nanticoke River\n        </a>\n        southwest of\n        <a href="/wiki/Seaford,_Delaware" title="Seaford, Delaware">\n         Seaford\n        </a>\n        .\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        <a href="/wiki/Forts_Ferry_Crossing" title="Forts Ferry Crossing">\n         Forts Ferry Crossing\n        </a>\n        connects\n        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Delaware_City" title="Delaware City">\n         Delaware City\n        </a>\n        with\n        <a href="/wiki/Fort_Delaware" title="Fort Delaware">\n         Fort Delaware\n        </a>\n        and\n        <a href="/wiki/Fort_Mott_(New_Jersey)" title="Fort Mott (New Jersey)">\n         Fort Mott\n        </a>\n        , New Jersey\n       </li>\n      </ul>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Rail_and_bus">\n        Rail and bus\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="thumb tleft">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Wilmington_Station_from_parking_garage,_July_2014.JPG">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3240" data-file-width="4320" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7d/Wilmington_Station_from_parking_garage%2C_July_2014.JPG/220px-Wilmington_Station_from_parking_garage%2C_July_2014.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7d/Wilmington_Station_from_parking_garage%2C_July_2014.JPG/330px-Wilmington_Station_from_parking_garage%2C_July_2014.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7d/Wilmington_Station_from_parking_garage%2C_July_2014.JPG/440px-Wilmington_Station_from_parking_garage%2C_July_2014.JPG 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Wilmington_Station_from_parking_garage,_July_2014.JPG" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         Wilmington Station\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       <a href="/wiki/Amtrak" title="Amtrak">\n        Amtrak\n       </a>\n       has two stations in Delaware along the\n       <a href="/wiki/Northeast_Corridor" title="Northeast Corridor">\n        Northeast Corridor\n       </a>\n       ; the relatively quiet\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Newark_Rail_Station_(Delaware)" title="Newark Rail Station (Delaware)">\n        Newark Rail Station\n       </a>\n       in Newark, and the busier\n       <a href="/wiki/Wilmington_station_(Delaware)" title="Wilmington station (Delaware)">\n        Wilmington Rail Station\n       </a>\n       in Wilmington. The Northeast Corridor is also served by\n       <a href="/wiki/SEPTA" title="SEPTA">\n        SEPTA\n       </a>\n       \'s\n       <a href="/wiki/Wilmington/Newark_Line" title="Wilmington/Newark Line">\n        Wilmington/Newark Line\n       </a>\n       of\n       <a href="/wiki/SEPTA_Regional_Rail" title="SEPTA Regional Rail">\n        Regional Rail\n       </a>\n       , which serves\n       <a href="/wiki/Claymont,_Delaware" title="Claymont, Delaware">\n        Claymont\n       </a>\n       , Wilmington,\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Churchmans_Crossing,_Delaware" title="Churchmans Crossing, Delaware">\n        Churchmans Crossing\n       </a>\n       , and Newark.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Two\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Class_I_railroad" title="Class I railroad">\n        Class I railroads\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Norfolk_Southern" title="Norfolk Southern">\n        Norfolk Southern\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/CSX" title="CSX">\n        CSX\n       </a>\n       , provide freight rail service in northern New Castle County. Norfolk Southern provides freight service along the Northeast Corridor and to industrial areas in\n       <a href="/wiki/Edgemoor,_Delaware" title="Edgemoor, Delaware">\n        Edgemoor\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/New_Castle,_Delaware" title="New Castle, Delaware">\n        New Castle\n       </a>\n       , and\n       <a href="/wiki/Delaware_City,_Delaware" title="Delaware City, Delaware">\n        Delaware City\n       </a>\n       . CSX\'s\n       <a href="/wiki/Philadelphia_Subdivision" title="Philadelphia Subdivision">\n        Philadelphia Subdivision\n       </a>\n       passes through northern New Castle County parallel to the Amtrak Northeast Corridor. Multiple\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Short-line_railroad" title="Short-line railroad">\n        short-line railroads\n       </a>\n       provide freight service in Delaware. The\n       <a href="/wiki/Delmarva_Central_Railroad" title="Delmarva Central Railroad">\n        Delmarva Central Railroad\n       </a>\n       operates the most trackage of the short-line railroads, running from an interchange with Norfolk Southern in\n       <a href="/wiki/Porter,_Delaware" title="Porter, Delaware">\n        Porter\n       </a>\n       south through\n       <a href="/wiki/Dover,_Delaware" title="Dover, Delaware">\n        Dover\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Harrington,_Delaware" title="Harrington, Delaware">\n        Harrington\n       </a>\n       , and\n       <a href="/wiki/Seaford,_Delaware" title="Seaford, Delaware">\n        Seaford\n       </a>\n       to\n       <a href="/wiki/Delmar,_Delaware" title="Delmar, Delaware">\n        Delmar\n       </a>\n       , with another line running from Harrington to\n       <a href="/wiki/Frankford,_Delaware" title="Frankford, Delaware">\n        Frankford\n       </a>\n       . The Delmarva Central Railroad connects with two shortline railroads, the\n       <a href="/wiki/Delaware_Coast_Line_Railroad" title="Delaware Coast Line Railroad">\n        Delaware Coast Line Railroad\n       </a>\n       and the\n       <a href="/wiki/Maryland_and_Delaware_Railroad" title="Maryland and Delaware Railroad">\n        Maryland and Delaware Railroad\n       </a>\n       , which serve local customers in Sussex County.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-dcr_80-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-dcr-80">\n         [78]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       CSX connects with the freight/\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Heritage_railroad" title="Heritage railroad">\n        heritage\n       </a>\n       operation, the\n       <a href="/wiki/Wilmington_and_Western_Railroad" title="Wilmington and Western Railroad">\n        Wilmington and Western Railroad\n       </a>\n       , based in Wilmington and the\n       <a href="/wiki/East_Penn_Railroad" title="East Penn Railroad">\n        East Penn Railroad\n       </a>\n       , which operates a line from Wilmington to\n       <a href="/wiki/Coatesville,_Pennsylvania" title="Coatesville, Pennsylvania">\n        Coatesville, Pennsylvania\n       </a>\n       .\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The last north-south passenger train through the main part of Delaware was the\n       <a href="/wiki/Pennsylvania_Railroad" title="Pennsylvania Railroad">\n        Pennsylvania Railroad\n       </a>\n       \'s\n       <i>\n        The Cavalier,\n       </i>\n       which ended service from Philadelphia through the state\'s interior in 1951.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-81">\n        <a href="#cite_note-81">\n         [79]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Air">\n        Air\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       See also:\n       <a href="/wiki/Aviation_in_Delaware" title="Aviation in Delaware">\n        Aviation in Delaware\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       As of 2016\n       <sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;">\n        <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Delaware&amp;action=edit">\n         [update]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       , there is no scheduled air service from any Delaware airport, as has been the case in various years since 1991. Various airlines had served\n       <a href="/wiki/Wilmington_Airport_(Delaware)" title="Wilmington Airport (Delaware)">\n        Wilmington Airport\n       </a>\n       , with the latest departure being\n       <a href="/wiki/Frontier_Airlines" title="Frontier Airlines">\n        Frontier Airlines\n       </a>\n       in April 2015.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-82">\n        <a href="#cite_note-82">\n         [80]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Delaware is centrally situated in the\n       <a href="/wiki/Northeast_megalopolis" title="Northeast megalopolis">\n        Northeast megalopolis\n       </a>\n       region of cities along\n       <a href="/wiki/Interstate_95" title="Interstate 95">\n        I-95\n       </a>\n       . Therefore, Delaware\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Commercial_airline" title="Commercial airline">\n        commercial airline\n       </a>\n       passengers most frequently use\n       <a href="/wiki/Philadelphia_International_Airport" title="Philadelphia International Airport">\n        Philadelphia International Airport\n       </a>\n       (PHL),\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Baltimore-Washington_International_Thurgood_Marshall_Airport" title="Baltimore-Washington International Thurgood Marshall Airport">\n        Baltimore-Washington International Thurgood Marshall Airport\n       </a>\n       (BWI) and\n       <a href="/wiki/Washington_Dulles_International_Airport" title="Washington Dulles International Airport">\n        Washington Dulles International Airport\n       </a>\n       (IAD) for domestic and international transit. Residents of Sussex County will also use\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Wicomico_Regional_Airport" title="Wicomico Regional Airport">\n        Wicomico Regional Airport\n       </a>\n       (SBY), as it is located less than 10 miles (16\xc2\xa0km) from the Delaware border.\n       <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_City_International_Airport" title="Atlantic City International Airport">\n        Atlantic City International Airport\n       </a>\n       (ACY),\n       <a href="/wiki/Newark_Liberty_International_Airport" title="Newark Liberty International Airport">\n        Newark Liberty International Airport\n       </a>\n       (EWR), and\n       <a href="/wiki/Ronald_Reagan_Washington_National_Airport" title="Ronald Reagan Washington National Airport">\n        Ronald Reagan Washington National Airport\n       </a>\n       (DCA) are also within a 100-mile (160\xc2\xa0km) radius of New Castle County.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The\n       <a href="/wiki/Dover_Air_Force_Base" title="Dover Air Force Base">\n        Dover Air Force Base\n       </a>\n       of the Air Mobility Command is located in the central part of the state, and it is the home of the\n       <a href="/wiki/436th_Airlift_Wing" title="436th Airlift Wing">\n        436th Airlift Wing\n       </a>\n       and the\n       <a href="/wiki/512th_Airlift_Wing" title="512th Airlift Wing">\n        512th Airlift Wing\n       </a>\n       .\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Other general aviation airports in Delaware include\n       <a href="/wiki/Summit_Airport_(Delaware)" title="Summit Airport (Delaware)">\n        Summit Airport\n       </a>\n       near\n       <a href="/wiki/Middletown,_Delaware" title="Middletown, Delaware">\n        Middletown\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Delaware_Airpark" title="Delaware Airpark">\n        Delaware Airpark\n       </a>\n       near\n       <a href="/wiki/Cheswold,_Delaware" title="Cheswold, Delaware">\n        Cheswold\n       </a>\n       , and\n       <a href="/wiki/Delaware_Coastal_Airport" title="Delaware Coastal Airport">\n        Delaware Coastal Airport\n       </a>\n       near\n       <a href="/wiki/Georgetown,_Delaware" title="Georgetown, Delaware">\n        Georgetown\n       </a>\n       .\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Law_and_government">\n        Law and government\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <p>\n       Delaware\'s fourth and current constitution, adopted in 1897, provides for executive, judicial and legislative branches.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-83">\n        <a href="#cite_note-83">\n         [81]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Legislative_branch">\n        Legislative branch\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Delaware_State_Capitol.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1200" data-file-width="1600" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1b/Delaware_State_Capitol.jpg/220px-Delaware_State_Capitol.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1b/Delaware_State_Capitol.jpg/330px-Delaware_State_Capitol.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1b/Delaware_State_Capitol.jpg/440px-Delaware_State_Capitol.jpg 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Delaware_State_Capitol.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         The\n         <a href="/wiki/Delaware_General_Assembly" title="Delaware General Assembly">\n          Delaware General Assembly\n         </a>\n         meets in the\n         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Delaware_State_Capitol" title="Delaware State Capitol">\n          Legislative Hall\n         </a>\n         in\n         <a href="/wiki/Dover,_Delaware" title="Dover, Delaware">\n          Dover\n         </a>\n         .\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       The\n       <a href="/wiki/Delaware_General_Assembly" title="Delaware General Assembly">\n        Delaware General Assembly\n       </a>\n       consists of a\n       <a href="/wiki/Delaware_House_of_Representatives" title="Delaware House of Representatives">\n        House of Representatives\n       </a>\n       with 41 members and a\n       <a href="/wiki/Delaware_Senate" title="Delaware Senate">\n        Senate\n       </a>\n       with 21 members. It sits in Dover, the state capital. Representatives are elected to two-year terms, while senators are elected to four-year terms. The Senate confirms judicial and other nominees appointed by the governor.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Delaware\'s U.S. Senators are\n       <a href="/wiki/Tom_Carper" title="Tom Carper">\n        Tom Carper\n       </a>\n       (Democrat) and\n       <a href="/wiki/Chris_Coons" title="Chris Coons">\n        Chris Coons\n       </a>\n       (Democrat). Delaware\'s single U.S. Representative is\n       <a href="/wiki/Lisa_Blunt_Rochester" title="Lisa Blunt Rochester">\n        Lisa Blunt Rochester\n       </a>\n       (Democrat).\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Judicial_branch">\n        Judicial branch\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <p>\n       The Delaware Constitution establishes a number of courts:\n      </p>\n      <ul>\n       <li>\n        The\n        <a href="/wiki/Delaware_Supreme_Court" title="Delaware Supreme Court">\n         Delaware Supreme Court\n        </a>\n        is the state\'s highest court.\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        The\n        <a href="/wiki/Delaware_Superior_Court" title="Delaware Superior Court">\n         Delaware Superior Court\n        </a>\n        is the state\'s trial court of general jurisdiction.\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        The\n        <a href="/wiki/Delaware_Court_of_Chancery" title="Delaware Court of Chancery">\n         Delaware Court of Chancery\n        </a>\n        deals primarily in corporate disputes.\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        The Family Court handles domestic and custody matters.\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        The\n        <a href="/wiki/Delaware_Court_of_Common_Pleas" title="Delaware Court of Common Pleas">\n         Delaware Court of Common Pleas\n        </a>\n        has jurisdiction over a limited class of civil and criminal matters.\n       </li>\n      </ul>\n      <p>\n       Minor non-constitutional courts include the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Justice_of_the_Peace" title="Justice of the Peace">\n        Justice of the Peace\n       </a>\n       Courts and Aldermen\'s Courts.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Significantly, Delaware has one of the few remaining Courts of\n       <a href="/wiki/Court_of_equity" title="Court of equity">\n        Chancery\n       </a>\n       in the nation, which has jurisdiction over\n       <a href="/wiki/Equity_(law)" title="Equity (law)">\n        equity\n       </a>\n       cases, the vast majority of which are corporate disputes, many relating to\n       <a href="/wiki/Mergers_and_acquisitions" title="Mergers and acquisitions">\n        mergers and acquisitions\n       </a>\n       . The\n       <a href="/wiki/Delaware_Court_of_Chancery" title="Delaware Court of Chancery">\n        Court of Chancery\n       </a>\n       and the Delaware Supreme Court have developed a worldwide reputation for rendering concise opinions concerning\n       <a href="/wiki/Corporate_law" title="Corporate law">\n        corporate law\n       </a>\n       which generally (but not always) grant broad discretion to corporate boards of directors and officers. In addition, the\n       <a href="/wiki/Delaware_General_Corporation_Law" title="Delaware General Corporation Law">\n        Delaware General Corporation Law\n       </a>\n       , which forms the basis of the Courts\' opinions, is widely regarded as giving great flexibility to corporations to manage their affairs. For these reasons, Delaware is considered to have the most business-friendly legal system in the United States; therefore a great number of companies are\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Incorporated_in_Delaware" title="Incorporated in Delaware">\n        incorporated in Delaware\n       </a>\n       , including 60% of the companies listed on the\n       <a href="/wiki/New_York_Stock_Exchange" title="New York Stock Exchange">\n        New York Stock Exchange\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-divcorpabout_84-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-divcorpabout-84">\n         [82]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Delaware was the last US state to use\n       <a href="/wiki/Judicial_corporal_punishment" title="Judicial corporal punishment">\n        judicial corporal punishment\n       </a>\n       , in 1952.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-85">\n        <a href="#cite_note-85">\n         [83]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Executive_branch">\n        Executive branch\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       See also:\n       <a href="/wiki/List_of_Governors_of_Delaware" title="List of Governors of Delaware">\n        List of Governors of Delaware\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       The executive branch is headed by the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Governor_of_Delaware" title="Governor of Delaware">\n        Governor of Delaware\n       </a>\n       . The present governor is\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/John_C._Carney_Jr." title="John C. Carney Jr.">\n        John Carney\n       </a>\n       (Democrat), who took office January 20, 2009. The lieutenant governor is\n       <a href="/wiki/Bethany_Hall-Long" title="Bethany Hall-Long">\n        Bethany Hall-Long\n       </a>\n       . The governor presents a "\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/State_of_the_State" title="State of the State">\n        State of the State\n       </a>\n       " speech to a\n       <a href="/wiki/Joint_session" title="Joint session">\n        joint session\n       </a>\n       of the Delaware legislature annually.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-86">\n        <a href="#cite_note-86">\n         [84]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Counties">\n        Counties\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <p>\n       Delaware is subdivided into\n       <a href="/wiki/List_of_counties_in_Delaware" title="List of counties in Delaware">\n        three counties\n       </a>\n       ; from north to south they are\n       <a href="/wiki/New_Castle_County,_Delaware" title="New Castle County, Delaware">\n        New Castle\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Kent_County,_Delaware" title="Kent County, Delaware">\n        Kent\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Sussex_County,_Delaware" title="Sussex County, Delaware">\n        Sussex\n       </a>\n       . This is the fewest among all states. Each county elects its own legislative body (known in New Castle and Sussex counties as\n       <b>\n        County Council\n       </b>\n       , and in Kent County as\n       <b>\n        Levy Court\n       </b>\n       ), which deal primarily in zoning and development issues. Most functions which are handled on a county-by-county basis in other states \xe2\x80\x93 such as court and law enforcement \xe2\x80\x93 have been centralized in Delaware, leading to a significant concentration of power in the Delaware state government. The counties were historically divided into\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hundred_(country_subdivision)" title="Hundred (country subdivision)">\n        hundreds\n       </a>\n       , which were used as tax reporting and voting districts until the 1960s, but now serve no administrative role, their only current official legal use being in real-estate title descriptions.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-87">\n        <a href="#cite_note-87">\n         [85]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Politics">\n        Politics\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       See also:\n       <a href="/wiki/United_States_presidential_election_in_Delaware,_2016" title="United States presidential election in Delaware, 2016">\n        United States presidential election in Delaware, 2016\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Political_party_strength_in_Delaware" title="Political party strength in Delaware">\n        Political party strength in Delaware\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <table class="wikitable" style="float:right; Until the\n       <a href="/wiki/United_States_presidential_election,_2000" title="United States presidential election, 2000">\n        2000 presidential election\n       </a>\n       , the state tended to be a Presidential\n       <a href="/wiki/Bellwether" title="Bellwether">\n        bellwether\n       </a>\n       , sending its three\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Electoral_votes" title="Electoral votes">\n        electoral votes\n       </a>\n       to the winning candidate since 1952. This trend ended in 2000 when Delaware\'s electoral votes went to\n       <a href="/wiki/Al_Gore" title="Al Gore">\n        Al Gore\n       </a>\n       . In 2004\n       <a href="/wiki/John_Kerry" title="John Kerry">\n        John Kerry\n       </a>\n       won Delaware by eight percentage points. In 2008 Democrat\n       <a href="/wiki/Barack_Obama" title="Barack Obama">\n        Barack Obama\n       </a>\n       defeated Republican\n       <a href="/wiki/John_McCain" title="John McCain">\n        John McCain\n       </a>\n       in Delaware 62.63% to 37.37%. Obama\'s\n       <a href="/wiki/Running_mate" title="Running mate">\n        running mate\n       </a>\n       was\n       <a href="/wiki/Joe_Biden" title="Joe Biden">\n        Joe Biden\n       </a>\n       , who had represented Delaware in the\n       <a href="/wiki/United_States_Senate" title="United States Senate">\n        United States Senate\n       </a>\n       since 1973. Obama carried Delaware again in 2012. In 2016, Delaware\'s electoral votes went to\n       <a href="/wiki/Hillary_Clinton" title="Hillary Clinton">\n        Hillary Clinton\n       </a>\n       .\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Delaware\'s swing to the Democrats is in part due to a strong Democratic trend in New Castle County, home to 55 percent of Delaware\'s population (the two smaller counties have only 359,000 people between them to New Castle\'s 535,000). New Castle has not voted Republican in a presidential election since 1988. In 1992, 2000, 2004, and 2016, the Republican presidential candidate carried both Kent and Sussex but lost by double-digits each time in New Castle, which was a large enough margin to swing the state to the Democrats. New Castle also elects a substantial majority of the legislature; 27 of the 41 state house districts and 14 of the 21 state senate districts are based in New Castle.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The Democrats have held the governorship since 1993, having won the last six gubernatorial elections in a row. Democrats presently hold seven of the nine statewide elected offices, while the Republicans hold only two statewide offices,\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/State_Auditor" title="State Auditor">\n        State Auditor\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/State_Treasurer" title="State Treasurer">\n        State Treasurer\n       </a>\n       .\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Freedom_of_information">\n        Freedom of information\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       See also:\n       <a href="/wiki/Freedom_of_information_in_the_United_States#State_legislation" title="Freedom of information in the United States">\n        Freedom of information in the United States \xc2\xa7\xc2\xa0State legislation\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       Each of the 50 states of the United States has passed some form of freedom of information legislation, which provides a mechanism for the general public to request information of the government.\n       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">\n        [\n        <i>\n         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">\n          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2011)">\n           citation needed\n          </span>\n         </a>\n        </i>\n        ]\n       </sup>\n       In 2011 Delaware passed legislation placing a 15 business day time limit on addressing freedom-of-information requests, to either produce information or an explanation of why such information would take longer than this time to produce.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-88">\n        <a href="#cite_note-88">\n         [86]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Government_revenue">\n        Government revenue\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <p>\n       Delaware has six different\n       <a href="/wiki/Income_tax" title="Income tax">\n        income tax\n       </a>\n       brackets, ranging from 2.2% to 5.95%. The state does not assess\n       <a href="/wiki/Sales_tax" title="Sales tax">\n        sales tax\n       </a>\n       on consumers. The state does, however, impose a tax on the gross receipts of most businesses. Business and occupational license tax rates range from 0.096% to 1.92%, depending on the category of business activity.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Delaware does not assess a state-level tax on real or personal property. Real estate is subject to county\n       <a href="/wiki/Property_tax" title="Property tax">\n        property taxes\n       </a>\n       , school district property taxes, vocational school district taxes, and, if located within an incorporated area, municipal property taxes.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       <a href="/wiki/Gambling_in_the_United_States#Authorized_types" title="Gambling in the United States">\n        Gambling\n       </a>\n       provides significant revenue to the state. For instance, the\n       <a href="/wiki/Delaware_Park_Racetrack#Casino" title="Delaware Park Racetrack">\n        casino at Delaware Park Racetrack\n       </a>\n       provided more than $100 million USD to the state in 2010.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-89">\n        <a href="#cite_note-89">\n         [87]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Voter_Registration">\n        Voter Registration\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <table class="wikitable">\n       <tr>\n        <th colspan="6">\n         Voter 697,769\n        </th>\n        <th style="text-align:center;">\n         100%\n        </th>\n       </tr>\n      </table>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Municipalities">\n        Municipalities\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <p>\n       Wilmington is the state\'s largest city and its economic hub. It is located within commuting distance of both Philadelphia and Baltimore. All regions of Delaware are enjoying phenomenal growth, with Dover and the beach resorts expanding at a rapid rate.\n      </p>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n locations by per capita income\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Education">\n        Education\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:UDel_Memorial_and_Magnolia_Circle.JPG">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1952" data-file-width="2608" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/36/UDel_Memorial_and_Magnolia_Circle.JPG/220px-UDel_Memorial_and_Magnolia_Circle.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/36/UDel_Memorial_and_Magnolia_Circle.JPG/330px-UDel_Memorial_and_Magnolia_Circle.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/36/UDel_Memorial_and_Magnolia_Circle.JPG/440px-UDel_Memorial_and_Magnolia_Circle.JPG 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:UDel_Memorial_and_Magnolia_Circle.JPG" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         University of Delaware\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       Delaware was the origin of\n       <i>\n        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Belton_v._Gebhart" title="Belton v. Gebhart">\n         Belton v. Gebhart\n        </a>\n       </i>\n       , one of the four cases which was combined into\n       <i>\n        <a href="/wiki/Brown_v._Board_of_Education" title="Brown v. Board of Education">\n         Brown v. Board of Education\n        </a>\n       </i>\n       , the\n       <a href="/wiki/Supreme_Court_of_the_United_States" title="Supreme Court of the United States">\n        Supreme Court of the United States\n       </a>\n       decision that led to the end of\n       <a href="/wiki/Racial_segregation" title="Racial segregation">\n        segregated\n       </a>\n       public schools. Significantly,\n       <i>\n        Belton\n       </i>\n       was the only case in which the state court found for the plaintiffs, thereby ruling that segregation was unconstitutional.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Unlike many states, Delaware\'s educational system is centralized in a state Superintendent of Education, with local school boards retaining control over taxation and some curriculum decisions.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       As of 2011\n       <sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;">\n        <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Delaware&amp;action=edit">\n         [update]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       , the Delaware Department of Education had authorized the founding of 25\n       <a href="/wiki/Charter_school" title="Charter school">\n        charter schools\n       </a>\n       in the state, one of them being\n       <a href="/wiki/Single-sex_education" title="Single-sex education">\n        all-girls\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Dobo20110612_91-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Dobo20110612-91">\n         [89]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       All teachers in the State\'s public school districts are unionized.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-dobo2012_92-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-dobo2012-92">\n         [90]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       As of January 2012\n       <sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;">\n        <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Delaware&amp;action=edit">\n         [update]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       , none of the State\'s charter schools are members of a teachers\n       <a href="/wiki/Trade_union" title="Trade union">\n        union\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-dobo2012_92-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-dobo2012-92">\n         [90]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       One of the State\'s teachers\' unions is Delaware State Education Association (DSEA), whose President as of January 2012 is Frederika Jenner.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-dobo2012_92-2">\n        <a href="#cite_note-dobo2012-92">\n         [90]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Colleges_and_Universities">\n        Colleges and Universities\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <ul>\n       <li>\n        <a <li>\n        <a href="/wiki/Drexel_University" title="Drexel University">\n         Drexel University\n        </a>\n        at Wilmington\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        <a class="mw-redirect"  2018)\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        <a href="/wiki/Wesley_College_(Delaware)" title="Wesley College (Delaware)">\n         Wesley College\n        </a>\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        <a href="/wiki/Wilmington_University" title="Wilmington University">\n         Wilmington University\n        </a>\n       </li>\n      </ul>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Sister_cities_and_states">\n        Sister cities and states\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <p>\n       Delaware\'s\n       <a href="/wiki/Paradiplomacy#United_States" title="Paradiplomacy">\n        sister state\n       </a>\n       in Japan is\n       <a href="/wiki/Miyagi_Prefecture" title="Miyagi Prefecture">\n        Miyagi Prefecture\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-93">\n        <a href="#cite_note-93">\n         [91]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Media">\n        Media\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <table class="plainlinks metadata ambox mbox-small-left ambox-content" role="presentation">\n       <tr>\n        <td class="mbox-image">\n         <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg">\n          <img alt="[icon]" data-file-height="31" data-file-width="44" height="14" also:\n       <a href="/wiki/Category:Delaware_media" title="Category:Delaware media">\n        Category:Delaware media\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Television">\n        Television\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <p>\n       The northern part of the state is served by network stations in\n       <a href="/wiki/Philadelphia" title="Philadelphia">\n        Philadelphia\n       </a>\n       and the southern part by network stations in\n       <a href="/wiki/Baltimore" title="Baltimore">\n        Baltimore\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Salisbury,_Maryland" title="Salisbury, Maryland">\n        Salisbury, Maryland\n       </a>\n       . Philadelphia\'s\n       <a href="/wiki/American_Broadcasting_Company" title="American Broadcasting Company">\n        ABC\n       </a>\n       affiliate,\n       <a href="/wiki/WPVI-TV" title="WPVI-TV">\n        WPVI-TV\n       </a>\n       , maintains a news bureau in downtown Wilmington. Salisbury\'s\n       <a href="/wiki/American_Broadcasting_Company" title="American Broadcasting Company">\n        ABC\n       </a>\n       affiliate,\n       <a href="/wiki/WMDT" title="WMDT">\n        WMDT\n       </a>\n       covers Sussex and lower Kent County; while\n       <a href="/wiki/CBS" title="CBS">\n        CBS\n       </a>\n       affiliate,\n       <a href="/wiki/WBOC-TV" title="WBOC-TV">\n        WBOC-TV\n       </a>\n       , maintains bureaus in Dover and Milton.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Few television stations are based solely in Delaware; the local\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Public_Broadcasting_Service" title="Public Broadcasting Service">\n        PBS\n       </a>\n       station from Philadelphia (but licensed to Wilmington),\n       <a href="/wiki/WHYY-TV" title="WHYY-TV">\n        WHYY-TV\n       </a>\n       , maintains a studio and broadcasting facility in Wilmington and Dover,\n       <a href="/wiki/Ion_Television" title="Ion Television">\n        Ion Television\n       </a>\n       affiliate\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/WPPX" title="WPPX">\n        WPPX\n       </a>\n       is licensed to Wilmington but maintains their offices in Philadelphia and their digital transmitter outside of that city and an analog tower in New Jersey, and\n       <a href="/wiki/MeTV" title="MeTV">\n        MeTV\n       </a>\n       affiliate\n       <a href="/wiki/KJWP" title="KJWP">\n        KJWP\n       </a>\n       is licensed to Wilmington but maintains their offices in New Jersey and their transmitter is located at the antenna farm in Philadelphia.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       In April 2014, it was revealed that\n       <a href="/wiki/Rehoboth_Beach,_Delaware" title="Rehoboth Beach, Delaware">\n        Rehoboth Beach\n       </a>\n       \'s\n       <a href="/wiki/WRDE-LD" title="WRDE-LD">\n        WRDE-LD\n       </a>\n       would affiliate with\n       <a href="/wiki/NBC" title="NBC">\n        NBC\n       </a>\n       , becoming the first major network-affiliated station in Delaware.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mcn-coasttv_94-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-mcn-coasttv-94">\n         [92]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Tourism">\n        Tourism\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Rehoboth_Beach_at_Delaware_Avenue.JPG">\n         <img alt="" //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/39/Rehoboth_Beach_at_Delaware_Avenue.JPG/400px-Rehoboth_Beach_at_Delaware_Avenue.JPG 2x" width="200"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Rehoboth_Beach_at_Delaware_Avenue.JPG" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         Rehoboth Beach is a popular vacation spot during the summer months\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Fort_Delaware_LOC_384066pu.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3025" data-file-width="3867" height="156" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7c/Fort_Delaware_LOC_384066pu.jpg/200px-Fort_Delaware_LOC_384066pu.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7c/Fort_Delaware_LOC_384066pu.jpg/300px-Fort_Delaware_LOC_384066pu.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7c/Fort_Delaware_LOC_384066pu.jpg/400px-Fort_Delaware_LOC_384066pu.jpg 2x" width="200"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Fort_Delaware_LOC_384066pu.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         <a href="/wiki/Fort_Delaware_State_Park" title="Fort Delaware State Park">\n          Fort Delaware State Park\n         </a>\n         on Pea Patch Island is a popular spot during the spring and summer. A ferry takes visitors to the fort from nearby\n         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Delaware_City" title="Delaware City">\n          Delaware City\n         </a>\n         .\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       In addition to\n       <a href="/wiki/First_State_National_Historical_Park" title="First State National Historical Park">\n        First State National Historical Park\n       </a>\n       , Delaware has several\n       <a href="/wiki/List_of_museums_in_Delaware" title="List of museums in Delaware">\n        museums\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Category:National_Wildlife_Refuges_in_Delaware" title="Category:National Wildlife Refuges in Delaware">\n        wildlife refuges\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Category:Parks_in_Delaware" title="Category:Parks in Delaware">\n        parks\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Category:Houses_in_Delaware" title="Category:Houses in Delaware">\n        houses\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Category:Lighthouses_in_Delaware" title="Category:Lighthouses in Delaware">\n        lighthouses\n       </a>\n       , and other\n       <a href="/wiki/Category:National_Register_of_Historic_Places_in_Delaware" title="Category:National Register of Historic Places in Delaware">\n        historic places\n       </a>\n       .\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       <a href="/wiki/Rehoboth_Beach,_Delaware" title="Rehoboth Beach, Delaware">\n        Rehoboth Beach\n       </a>\n       , together with the towns of\n       <a href="/wiki/Lewes,_Delaware" title="Lewes, Delaware">\n        Lewes\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Dewey_Beach,_Delaware" title="Dewey Beach, Delaware">\n        Dewey Beach\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Bethany_Beach,_Delaware" title="Bethany Beach, Delaware">\n        Bethany Beach\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/South_Bethany,_Delaware" title="South Bethany, Delaware">\n        South Bethany\n       </a>\n       , and\n       <a href="/wiki/Fenwick_Island,_Delaware" title="Fenwick Island, Delaware">\n        Fenwick Island\n       </a>\n       , comprise\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Delaware_beaches" title="Delaware beaches">\n        Delaware\'s beach resorts\n       </a>\n       . Rehoboth Beach often bills itself as "The Nation\'s Summer Capital" because it is a frequent summer vacation destination for Washington, D.C. residents as well as visitors from Maryland, Virginia, and in lesser numbers, Pennsylvania. Vacationers are drawn for many reasons, including the town\'s charm, artistic appeal, nightlife, and tax free shopping. According to SeaGrant Delaware, the Delaware Beaches generate $6.9 billion annually and over $711 million in tax revenue.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-95">\n        <a href="#cite_note-95">\n         [93]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Delaware is home to several festivals, fairs, and events. Some of the more notable festivals are the Riverfest held in\n       <a href="/wiki/Seaford,_Delaware" title="Seaford, Delaware">\n        Seaford\n       </a>\n       , the World Championship\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Punkin_Chunkin#World_Championship_Punkin_Chunkin" title="Punkin Chunkin">\n        Punkin Chunkin\n       </a>\n       held at various locations throughout the state since 1986, the Rehoboth Beach Chocolate Festival, the Bethany Beach Jazz Funeral to mark the end of summer, the Apple Scrapple Festival held in\n       <a href="/wiki/Bridgeville,_Delaware" title="Bridgeville, Delaware">\n        Bridgeville\n       </a>\n       , the\n       <a href="/wiki/Clifford_Brown" title="Clifford Brown">\n        Clifford Brown\n       </a>\n       Jazz Festival in Wilmington, the Rehoboth Beach Jazz Festival, the Sea Witch Halloween Festival and Parade in Rehoboth Beach, the Rehoboth Beach Independent Film Festival, the Nanticoke Indian Pow Wow in\n       <a href="/wiki/Oak_Orchard,_Delaware" title="Oak Orchard, Delaware">\n        Oak Orchard\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Firefly_Music_Festival" title="Firefly Music Festival">\n        Firefly Music Festival\n       </a>\n       , and the Return Day Parade held after every election in\n       <a href="/wiki/Georgetown,_Delaware" title="Georgetown, Delaware">\n        Georgetown\n       </a>\n       .\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Culture_and_entertainment">\n        Culture and entertainment\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Festivals">\n        Festivals\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       Main article:\n       <a href="/wiki/Delaware_festivals" title="Delaware festivals">\n        Delaware festivals\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Sports">\n        Sports\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <dl>\n       <dt>\n        Professional Teams\n       </dt>\n      </dl>\n      <table class="wikitable">\n       <tr>\n        <th>\n         Team\n        </th>\n
